On Wed, 2005-07-13 at 20:56 -0700, Russ Johnson wrote:

> According to what I was told by immigrations, the best documentation is 
> either your birth certificate or a passport.

The last time I crossed into Canada, they only asked for a driver's
license to look me up on their computer systems.  Crossing back in the
US, they only asked for a driver's license to look me up on their
computer system.  Granted, this was before the whole 9-11 incident and
they are prone to be more anal these days at the border.

Officially, I am sure, you will need proof of US Citizenship.  Which, in
our country, is either a passport or birth certificate.  And if you ask
the official channels, you will be told this.  And I am sure the border
guards could detain you if you fail to provide this documentation.  But
would you actually be detained if you only had a driver license?  I
would think probably not.

Coincidentally, Oregon is one of the few states that do not require you
to submit or show a valid US Birth Certificate or other documentation of
legal US residency to get a driver's license.  But I hear this may
change in the future, as the Patriot Act and its supporters apply
pressure.

Jason wrote:

>The last time I crossed into Canada, they only asked for a driver's
>license to look me up on their computer systems.  Crossing back in the
>US, they only asked for a driver's license to look me up on their
>computer system.  Granted, this was before the whole 9-11 incident and
>they are prone to be more anal these days at the border.
>  
>
March of this year, a DL was not "good enough". We had our drivers 
licenses (all four adults) in a non-descript Chevrolet Cavalier with 
plain Oregon plates. All four adults are related, and live at two 
different Oregon addresses. Nothing that should have been a red flag.

Yet we spent nearly an hour at the immigration office at the border 
because we did not have proof of citizenship.

Coming back into the US was actually easier than leaving, although, the 
first question our of the US border guards mouth after looking at our 
ODLs was, "And do you have proof of citizenship?"

>Officially, I am sure, you will need proof of US Citizenship.  Which, in
>our country, is either a passport or birth certificate.  And if you ask
>the official channels, you will be told this.
>
We asked prior to making our plans. We were told to bring "ID". We were 
not told to bring proof of citizenship. To me, my DL *IS* ID. I had no 
reason to think otherwise.

I happen to have birth certificates for all four adults, since two are 
my kids, and the other adult is their mother. As I said we're all related.

>  And I am sure the border
>guards could detain you if you fail to provide this documentation.  But
>would you actually be detained if you only had a driver license?  I
>would think probably not.
>  
>
Wrong. We were told to go to Immigration. The woman at immigration told 
us that if any of us had criminal convictions, we would be denied entry 
and escorted back across the border and placed in custody. The US border 
guards would then process us to determine if we were to be detained by 
US officials.

This is what the border offical told us, and I have no reason to doubt 
what she said. She did produce a sheet of paper with every traffic 
violation I had committed since I was 16. This at least proved that I'd 
been in the US for a while...

>Coincidentally, Oregon is one of the few states that do not require you
>to submit or show a valid US Birth Certificate or other documentation of
>legal US residency to get a driver's license.  But I hear this may
>change in the future, as the Patriot Act and its supporters apply
>pressure.
>  
>
It's already changing. The Oregon congress is hearing arguments and may 
change that law by the end of this session. I have no idea what this 
will require of present license holders. If they grandfather in present 
license holders, then the requirement is pretty bogus.

From wamorita at hevanet.com  Wed Jul 13 23:01:21 2005

Subject: [PLUG] FC4 Boot problem -- Resoved
Message-ID: <200507140601.j6E61MD77832@pop.hevanet.com>

I was having a problem booting the FC4 install disk.
It appears that FC4 thought I had RAID drives.
Solved the problem at the install disk boot with "linux pci=nosort"

Mandel said, "Given the current situation with LinuxFund, I may be
interested in becoming a part-time executive director. The goals and
procedures of LinuxFund need to be clarified and rethought in light of
changes in open source." Mandel thinks Linux Fund should be incorporated
into a larger, well-run non-profit, such as Portland's FreeGeek, which
is a successful hardware recycler and major FOSS proponent.

He also believes that LinuxFund's top priority should be distributing
the $126,000, that has accumulated since the project was largely
abandoned. "LinuxFund also needs to get a developer board together and
start giving out money," said Mandel. "I would be willing to help with
this."

> is a successful hardware recycler and major FOSS proponent.
> 
> He also believes that LinuxFund's top priority should be distributing
> the $126,000, that has accumulated since the project was largely
> abandoned. "LinuxFund also needs to get a developer board together and
> start giving out money," said Mandel. "I would be willing to help with
> this."

> Just out of curiosity, what class and what area of "Open Source" ?
> 
> "Open Source" is an extremeley broad term to use in this context... it
> means so much to so many.  :-)

> Rob
> _______________________________________________
> PLUG mailing list
> PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug
> 

The class is entitled "Open Source UNIX Software Development".
Basically, we have 8 weeks to work on almost ANY GPL'd project that we
want. In doing so, we get to familiarize our self with the open source
development in general (i.e. licenses, patches, IRC, sourceforge,
revision control...)

There is a wide variety of projects this term. One guy is writing a USB
ethernet driver, another is writing a clone of the NES Dragon Warrior
Game, and another is doing some work on a programmable electronic fuel
injection controller. I am getting credit for working with the Kernel
Janitor's in reducing the GCC4 Kernel build warnings.

It's a great class. And like you said, extremely broad and informal.
Hope to see you soon.

-- 
Jesse Millan
CNS Unix Team
Portland State University
Phone: (503) 725-9151
GPG key: www.system-calls.com/gpg.php

>From The Collaborative International Dictionary of English v.0.48
[gcide]:

  Inconceivable \In`con*ceiv"a*ble\, a. [Pref. in- not +
     conceivable: cf. F. inconcevable.]
     Not conceivable; incapable of being conceived by the mind;
     not explicable by the human intellect, or by any known
     principles or agencies; incomprehensible; as, it is
     inconceivable to us how the will acts in producing muscular
     motion.
     [1913 Webster]

>From WordNet (r) 2.0 [wn]:

  inconceivable
       adj : totally unlikely [syn: {impossible}, {out of the question},
             {unimaginable}]

From ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net  Fri Jul 15 08:57:01 2005
From: ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Fri, 15 Jul 2005 08:57:01 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Image file association in KDE
In-Reply-To: <200507150828.08578.rsteff@comcast.net>
References: <200507150828.08578.rsteff@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <200507150857.01180.ewilhelm@sbcglobal.net>

# from Richard C. Steffens
# on Friday 15 July 2005 08:28 am:

>now, instead of displaying the file,
>Konqueror asks me what program to use to open the file. Konqueror
> itself, is not on the list of programs to open an image.

You mean it's not in the "images" folder of your k-menu?  That doesn't 
really matter.  I don't think you can just type "konqueror" in the 
blank though (does that make a loop or no?)

>Any idea what I need to do to restore the default?

You need to enable the "embedded viewer".  There's another tab on the 
file-associations dialog.  This is what you get if you click on the 
image.  Middle-click may still send it to the external program which 
appears first in the list (like gimp.)  I think the behavior may have 
changed in some subtle way between versions.  I've had the same sort of 
confusion.

--Eric

From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)

Subject: [PLUG] Python Lists and File Reads
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.62.0507151522100.15022@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

   I had a function working when I specified the input file as "*.py" and
imported it as a list. However, I need to be able to use disk files with
various names as input, so I changed the code. The function broke (of
course!) and I cannot find a web page that gives me the appropriate methods
to use.

   Here's the function code:
===========================================================================
#!/usr/bin/python
"""
   Takes a list of components and creates an output file of all pairwise
   combinations of components.
"""
import sys
import pdb

pdb.set_trace()

def scopingpairs(input, output):

   input = open('sys.argv[1]', 'r')
   output = open('sys.argv[2]', 'a')

   pairwise = []
   src = input.read()

   for elem1 in src:
     for elem2 in src:
       if src.index(elem1) < src.index(elem2):
         pairwise.append((elem1, elem2))

   for index in range(len(pairwise)):
     output.write(str(pairwise[index])+'\n')

   input.close()
   output.close()
============================================================================

   Working interactively, (so I don't know that the open() syntax is correct
and working), the code works until it gets to the src.index(). Instead of
whole words being indexed, each character is indexed. I've tried putting the
input file as a list with quote delimited words, and as a string of quote
delimited words. Makes no difference.

   I've googled for "python list methods" but haven't hit anything relevant or
current. I can provide a sample data file if desired.

TIA,

Rich

Applied Ecosystem Services, Inc. (TM)  | Impact Assessments Using Fuzzy Logic"
<http://www.appl-ecosys.com>   Voice: 503-667-4517   Fax: 503-667-8863

Hash: SHA1

Rich Shepard wrote:
|   I had a function working when I specified the input file as "*.py" and
| imported it as a list. However, I need to be able to use disk files with
| various names as input, so I changed the code. The function broke (of
| course!) and I cannot find a web page that gives me the appropriate
methods
| to use.
|
|   Here's the function code:
|
===========================================================================
| #!/usr/bin/python
| """
|   Takes a list of components and creates an output file of all pairwise
|   combinations of components.
| """
| import sys
| import pdb
|
| pdb.set_trace()
|
| def scopingpairs(input, output):
|
|   input = open('sys.argv[1]', 'r')
|   output = open('sys.argv[2]', 'a')
~                  ^^^^^^^^^^^^^
I think you probably want to get rid of the quotes around both  of those
~ arguments.  Additionally, what's the point of passing "input" and
"output" as parameters if you never actually use the values?

| src = input.read()

This will read the entire input into a single string.
You probably meant to say:

src = input.read().split()

(Which will split the input string into an array using whitespace as a
delimiter).

Additionally, (assuming I read your intention correctly) your loop
probably makes more sense as:

- ----------------------------------
for i,elem1 in enumerate(src):
~  for j,elem2 in enumerate(src):
~   if i < j:
~     print >>output, (elem1,elem2)
- ----------------------------------

Or, alteratively:

- ----------------------------------
for i,elem1 in enumerate(src):
~  for elem2 in src[i+1:]:
~    print >>output, (elem1, elem2)
- -----------------------------------

> list. But, each item in the list has a terminating \n and I don't know how to

   Got it!

   fh = open('environ.in', 'r')
   input = fh.read().split()

   ... and input is a list with no newlines.

Excelsior!

Why are you using Python in the first place?  After having used Bash,
then a bit of perl, then a bit of C and C++, then python and a lot more
Perl, I really don't care much for Python.  It's not like the other kids.

I wouldn't jump in to a python project without a better grasp of the
language such how to manipulate strings or utilize functions and all
that jazz.  IMHO, perl is a much sharper tool for most jobs.

That said, Python is an interesting language that *is* quite useful for
many jobs... a lot of folks really love it and do amazing things with
it.  But if you're struggling with it, I'd suggest using something that
might be more familiar for you.  :-)

Rob,

   Well, I could do the whole thing in C. Python does eigenvectors and I'm not
sure that perl does. My need is for a mathematically-complete language with
the ability to easily build a GUI front end. The core libraries are in C
already.

   There are a ton of addons to python: Numeric/NumPy, SciPy, and so on. They
access LAPACK, BLAS, MatLab/Octave, S/S+ and R, and more.

   I understand the basics, it's the lack of current documentation on
implementation that frustrates me. Heck, I taught myself FORTRAN in the early
1970s using the horrible IBM S/360 manuals. I don't think the US Tax Code was
more obtuse than those manuals. (Try reading and understanding the -G, -H,
-WATFOR, and -WATFIV compilers using those old dogs.) C I found pretty easy;
eventually got my mind around pointers to pointers .... I certainly know the
OO concepts and how they work. I shouldn't have to spend hours of
trial-and-error to read data from a file and write data back out again. Sigh.
'Nuff venting; gotta' go.

1) We will be in the "build workshop area", which is the back room, and 
there will be signs.

2) Free Geek has monitors, mice, keyboards, patch cables, and network 
drops, so you don't have to bring any of that. If you're new to Linux and 
are doing a new install, then you should bring your own monitor (so that 
we get the settings right.)

3) I will grab a parking spot close to the Fair for a loading/unloading 
zone. Look for a large white sign that says "Linux Clinic unloading".

4) We're going to need some volunteers who are willing to take turns 
protecting the loading/unloading zone.

5) We will bring stickers and sharpies so you can label your equipment. 
It's always best to avoid misunderstandings. :)

6) Free Geek just got a thousand new Ubuntu disks and they're willing to 
share.

7) The Clinic session will only be from 1-4pm, but the Geek Fair runs from 
1-7pm. So everyone should have a chance to check-out the other activities.

at Free Geek this year too - Labor Day weekend. Definitely something to be

> On Tue, Jul 12, 2005 at 09:55:06PM -0700, Steve D... wrote:

> 
> Or vgetty, which is more likely to work with your modem:
> http://alpha.greenie.net/vgetty/
> 
> Modem compatibility database:
> http://mgetty.greenie.net/modembase/bin/overview.pl?language=en
> 
> _______________________________________________
> PLUG mailing list
> PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug

It looks like vgetty is a simpler package.  I looked into Asterisk,
but I don't think Asterisk is meant for what I'm after.  
I want to find a way to talk verbally over a dial-in connection 
so that any eavesdropper will hear a modem instead of the 
conversation.  I have mgetty pretty much figured out except for 
routing the ppp connection so that the person dialing into me 
can go beyond my server.  The modem isn't showing up as an 
interface.  Packets coming in through my modem seem to show up 
on my ethernet card.

As far as using vgetty for an answering machine implementation,
I guess I'll have to switch between mgetty and vgetty via cron.
The problem with the vgetty approach is that eavesdroppers will 
hear the conversation.  Ideally, I want to come up with some way 
to talk verbally over a dial-up TCP/IP connection.

I thought there was some way to set up mgetty and vgetty on the
same line, but I could be mistaken.  Isn't there some way for
the caller to send a code so that the server can choose between
mgetty and vgetty?

   --  Michael C. Robinson

From plug_0 at robinson-west.com  Fri Jul 15 13:36:42 2005
From: plug_0 at robinson-west.com (plug_0 at robinson-west.com)
Date: Fri, 15 Jul 2005 13:36:42 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Internetwork firewalling...
Message-ID: <1121459802.42d81e5a433d9@xerxes.robinson-west.com>

I have four networks...


     A ---- B ---- C
            |
            D

I want to allow ssh/scp from B to C, but not from C to B.  I want
to allow C to cross B without entering it to get to A.

So far I've used iptables DROP in the FORWARD chain on
B for packets from C destined to B or D.  I've also dropped 
all tcp and udp packets from C to B on B in the INPUT chain 
after explicitly allowing, time, dns and ssh packets.

If I can get packets to cross B and terminate somewhere in A
or beyond, I save an ip address on the A net.

The bind server on B can see the addresses for networks A-D, 
not just the ones for A and C.  Does Bind 9 offer a simple 
solution to limit the addresses that C can look up off of B?  
The server on B is a caching server fed off a primary and 
slave server in the B network.

I control the A-D networks.

     --  Michael C. Robinson

  # aptitude install libglu1-xorg

  # aptitude install xbase-clients

transition.  I presume that is responsible for the carnage.  When
the affected packages are rebuilt, I can reinstall.

From rsteff at comcast.net  Fri Jul 15 20:02:49 2005
From: rsteff at comcast.net (Richard C. Steffens)
Date: Fri, 15 Jul 2005 20:02:49 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Resolved: Image file association in KDE
In-Reply-To: <200507150857.01180.ewilhelm@sbcglobal.net>
References: <200507150828.08578.rsteff@comcast.net>
	<200507150857.01180.ewilhelm@sbcglobal.net>
Message-ID: <200507152002.49151.rsteff@comcast.net>

On Friday 15 July 2005 8:57 am, Eric Wilhelm wrote:
> # from Richard C. Steffens
>
> # on Friday 15 July 2005 08:28 am:
> >now, instead of displaying the file,
> >Konqueror asks me what program to use to open the file. Konqueror
> > itself, is not on the list of programs to open an image.

> You need to enable the "embedded viewer".  There's another tab on the
> file-associations dialog.  This is what you get if you click on the
> image.  Middle-click may still send it to the external program which
> appears first in the list (like gimp.)  I think the behavior may have
> changed in some subtle way between versions.  I've had the same sort of
> confusion.

Aha! Thanks. I missed that tab.

So, if this happens again, and I forget how to fix it, I can search the PLUG 
archives and find this:

In Konqueror, click on Settings, Configure Konqueror. Select File 
Associations, click on the plus next to Image, and select jpeg (or whatever 
image type for which might have messed up the association). Then click on the 
Embedding tab and click the radio button for "Show file in embedded viewer".

--

From mikeraz at patch.com  Sun Jul 17 19:26:00 2005
From: mikeraz at patch.com (Michael Rasmussen)
Date: Sun, 17 Jul 2005 19:26:00 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] RANT: Sofa King GUIs, Sofa King PKG Mgmt
Message-ID: <20050718022600.GA32163@patch.com>

Scenario #1 - A Tale of Two Package Management Systems

I run a mix of APT and RPM based systems.  I'll find the same functionality on both
system types, but supplied by different programs.  If I want the meta data from 
my digital camera photos I use exif on the apt systems and jhead on the RPM systems.

This got to be maddening enough in recalling the sytax to extract the information
that I finally just dumped them all and loaded Image::ExifTool from CPAN 

A quickie Perl program works on all my systems and is easy to munge to extract 
whatever information I need on a particular day for whatever purpose.

Scenario #2 - Pain in the GUI 

Discovering that the most recent set of install CDs on hand were from May 2004
I downloaded new ISOs to burn.  Fine, but since the last time I've burned a CD
I've upgraded xcdroast and it's broken.  It insists on trying to work with
/dev/pg and there's no (findable to my mind) to tell it and it's auto detection
stupidity to just use /dev/cdrom.  I can cut and paste the command line from the 
error log and replace the "dev =" and write CDs just fine.  

If I manually edit ~/.cdroast/xcdr098.cfg it will work.  But the point of a GUI is 
not to have users hand editing config files in hidden directories.


Scenario #3 - Auto Pretty Install is fine until ...

You reboot the machine and the mis-written GRUB config isn't bootable.  

Bah.

Beer time.


Thanks to the home brewer who named his beers "Sofa King Stout", "Sofa King IPA" and so
on.  He was a good enough brewer that three or four of his brews made it to the national
finals and won medals.  The American Homebrewer Association refused to print the names
of his beers in the awards list.  The next year all of his brews were named "You wouldn't
print it anyway STYLE".

From Jeff.Moore at chemeketa.edu  Mon Jul 18 09:31:52 2005
From: Jeff.Moore at chemeketa.edu (Jeff Moore)
Date: Mon, 18 Jul 2005 09:31:52 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Scriptless Portknocking
Message-ID: <4C7800EB52CF054BB0B4FF50968C1B6607CB70@cccmail2.chemeketa.network>

Hi all,

   Just saw this and had to share it with all of you.. 
   I have been interested in portknocking for a while now but hate the fact that you have to run scripts to check log files etc... It just seems clunky, at least for my needs. I only wanted to use it as an extra level of basic connection protection. You can really do some neat things with port knocking like sending encrypted passwords via icmp packets etc. But this wasnt what I was looking for. I just wanted something that would block John Q Scanner from seeing ssh open and then taking his time to try to crack it. Plus I didnt want to have to install a little script on every client to access the machines. 
   Well to make a long story short I ran accross this little fedora iptables entry:

-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -m state --state NEW -m tcp -p tcp --dport 22 -m recent --rcheck --name SSH -j ACCEPT
-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -m state --state NEW -m tcp -p tcp --dport 9022 -m recent --name SSH --remove -j DROP
-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -m state --state NEW -m tcp -p tcp --dport 9023 -m recent --name SSH --set -j DROP
-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -m state --state NEW -m tcp -p tcp --dport 9024 -m recent --name SSH --remove -j DROP

   I wasnt aware of the --name and --rcheck ability in IPTABLES. With these you can telnet to port 9023 (line3) and it will start tagging all packets from your host(and only your host) with the name SSH. Then you will be allowed to access port 22 (SSH) via the --rcheck (line1). When you are finished just telnet to 9022 or 9044 to stop tagging your traffic (closing the ssh port). One thing to note is the double entries for the shutdown. At first I wasnt sure why there were two then I though of scans.. Whether its a top down or bottom up scan it will always turn the naming off. 
   Sorry I just got so excited when I saw this. How elegant and powerful this is! 
   Hope you all enjoy it as much as I have...

Thanks for your time,
Jeff M.

From chaz at bctonline.com  Mon Jul 18 12:58:51 2005
From: chaz at bctonline.com (Charles Sliger)
Date: Mon, 18 Jul 2005 12:58:51 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Internetwork firewalling...
In-Reply-To: <1121459802.42d81e5a433d9@xerxes.robinson-west.com>

I think you are on the right track with iptables although I'd have to get
more specifics on the routers/firewalls within the 4 nets.
You speak of A-D both as nets and as systems so it's a little confusing.
(the INPUT chain controls traffic inbound to the firewall itself, not a
network)
I don't think you need to play with DNS to achieve your stated goals.
I'm pretty checked out on iptables and feel sure that with proper scripts
you should get the results you are looking for.
If you want me to look at any of it just let me know.

-----Original Message-----
From: plug-bounces at lists.pdxlinux.org
[mailto:plug-bounces at lists.pdxlinux.org] On Behalf Of
plug_0 at robinson-west.com
Sent: Friday, July 15, 2005 1:37 PM
To: plug at lists.pdxlinux.org
Subject: [PLUG] Internetwork firewalling...

I have four networks...


     A ---- B ---- C
            |
            D

I want to allow ssh/scp from B to C, but not from C to B.  I want
to allow C to cross B without entering it to get to A.

So far I've used iptables DROP in the FORWARD chain on
B for packets from C destined to B or D.  I've also dropped 
all tcp and udp packets from C to B on B in the INPUT chain 
after explicitly allowing, time, dns and ssh packets.

If I can get packets to cross B and terminate somewhere in A
or beyond, I save an ip address on the A net.

The bind server on B can see the addresses for networks A-D, 
not just the ones for A and C.  Does Bind 9 offer a simple 
solution to limit the addresses that C can look up off of B?  
The server on B is a caching server fed off a primary and 
slave server in the B network.

I control the A-D networks.

     --  Michael C. Robinson

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Mon Jul 18 20:59:38 2005
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Mon, 18 Jul 2005 20:59:38 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] OMR Scanner Need Resolved
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.62.0507182055160.3576@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

   As I washed the dinner dishes I thought of how to re-structure the form
I'll be  using. I can eliminate 7 bubble columns (leaving a total of 10) and
print it all on a page 82.5mm wide. We'll use a paper slicer to cut off the
excess.

   This width form will let me use a portable OMR reader that retails for $750
and can read up to 12 columns (plus 2 timing tracks). That's about the lowest
cost solution I've found. And, with TeX and PSTricks, printing the
appropriate size bubbles in exactly the right places is almost trivial; just
a lot of trial-and-error or very careful measuring.

Thanks all,

Rich

From nickaubert at gmail.com  Tue Jul 19 08:43:15 2005
From: nickaubert at gmail.com (Nick Aubert)
Date: Tue, 19 Jul 2005 08:43:15 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Kernel panic. Need help!!!
In-Reply-To: <1121774740.1030.2.camel@Balrog.jimwebb.net>
References: <1121774740.1030.2.camel@Balrog.jimwebb.net>

On 7/19/05, Jim Webb <jimwebb at charter.net> wrote:
> Hey people.  I just got the system to reboot.  I heard a noise that
> might be coming from the HD.  Would a bad HD cause what I saw?  If so,
> what can I do to get over to a new HD or what would you people suggest?

A failing hard drive could definitely cause a kernel panic.  So could
bad RAM, or any manner of other hardware problems.  But the noise from
the hard drive sounds like a giveaway.

I would suggest migrating any important data off of that drive as soon
as you get the chance.  Start with personal data: email archives,
photos, documents, any scripts you might have written, etc.  Unless
you've done a lot of heavy customization, I wouldn't recommend trying
to preserve the system itself.  Get a new hard drive, and upgrade from
RH 8 or 9 to FC 3 or 4.

-Nick

Dick, et al.:

   If the drive's flaky, it may not withstand another boot. My inclination
would be to format and partition a new drive in another machine, install
whatever distribution was desired, then network the two boxes (even if the
second one is borrowed just for the occasion) and copy across what's desired
to be saved. Then the current machine can be shut down, the hard drives
swapped, and the system rebooted.

-----Original Message-----
From: plug-bounces at lists.pdxlinux.org
[mailto:plug-bounces at lists.pdxlinux.org] On Behalf Of Jeff Moore
Sent: Monday, July 18, 2005 9:32 AM
To: plug at lists.pdxlinux.org
Subject: [PLUG] Scriptless Portknocking

Hi all,

   Just saw this and had to share it with all of you.. 
   I have been interested in portknocking for a while now but hate the fact
that you have to run scripts to check log files etc... It just seems clunky,
at least for my needs. I only wanted to use it as an extra level of basic
connection protection. You can really do some neat things with port knocking
like sending encrypted passwords via icmp packets etc. But this wasnt what I
was looking for. I just wanted something that would block John Q Scanner
from seeing ssh open and then taking his time to try to crack it. Plus I
didnt want to have to install a little script on every client to access the
machines. 
   Well to make a long story short I ran accross this little fedora iptables
entry:

-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -m state --state NEW -m tcp -p tcp --dport 22 -m
recent --rcheck --name SSH -j ACCEPT
-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -m state --state NEW -m tcp -p tcp --dport 9022 -m
recent --name SSH --remove -j DROP
-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -m state --state NEW -m tcp -p tcp --dport 9023 -m
recent --name SSH --set -j DROP
-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -m state --state NEW -m tcp -p tcp --dport 9024 -m
recent --name SSH --remove -j DROP

   I wasnt aware of the --name and --rcheck ability in IPTABLES. With these
you can telnet to port 9023 (line3) and it will start tagging all packets
from your host(and only your host) with the name SSH. Then you will be
allowed to access port 22 (SSH) via the --rcheck (line1). When you are
finished just telnet to 9022 or 9044 to stop tagging your traffic (closing
the ssh port). One thing to note is the double entries for the shutdown. At
first I wasnt sure why there were two then I though of scans.. Whether its a
top down or bottom up scan it will always turn the naming off. 
   Sorry I just got so excited when I saw this. How elegant and powerful
this is! 
   Hope you all enjoy it as much as I have...

Thanks for your time,
Jeff M.
_______________________________________________
PLUG mailing list
PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug

On Tue, 2005-07-19 at 08:43 -0700, Nick Aubert wrote:

> A failing hard drive could definitely cause a kernel panic.  So could
> bad RAM, or any manner of other hardware problems.  But the noise from
> the hard drive sounds like a giveaway.

Some of the tools on Knoppix can help. After backing up critical stuff
as suggested by others, you can use Knoppix to try backing up the entire
drive - I'd try the following commands (dd_rescue, in reverse read mode,
saved all of the data from a crunchy laptop drive about 4 months ago):

dd
dd_rescue

Mike

From Jeff.Moore at chemeketa.edu  Tue Jul 19 11:37:06 2005
From: Jeff.Moore at chemeketa.edu (Jeff Moore)
Date: Tue, 19 Jul 2005 11:37:06 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Re: Scriptless Portknocking (Jeff M)
Message-ID: <4C7800EB52CF054BB0B4FF50968C1B6607CB72@cccmail2.chemeketa.network>

Rob Wrote:
> Looks quite cool... and I'm in the same boat as you with regards to port
> knocking.  Now, are those iptables lines due to some Fedora weirdness or
> are they mainline?  :-)

Yeah thats correct. Its the /etc/sysconfig/iptables from fedora.. As far as I can tell the commands are valid iptables commands. I think fedora just uses its own naming convention "RH-Firewall-1" for the iptables chain. In most cases I think INPUT is used as the chain descriptor. One way to verify what your chains are is to do a "service iptables status" this will show you your chains, their names, and what rules are currently applied. If you replace the "RH-Firewall-1-INPUT" with the name of your chain and run "iptalbes $TestString" then it should apply your string to the running iptables. Then just do another status to verify that.
Sorry I am a bit of a noob at this. hope this helps.
JM

From alan at clueserver.org  Tue Jul 19 14:53:01 2005
From: alan at clueserver.org (Alan)
Date: Tue, 19 Jul 2005 14:53:01 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] ANNOUNCEMENT: Advanced Topics July 20th, 2005
Message-ID: <1121809981.19256.15.camel@dagon.fnordora.org>

Portland Linux/Unix Group Advanced Topics

Speaker:            Eric Wilhelm

Subject:            Rapid Development with a Safety Net
                 
Date:               July 20th 2005
Time:               7:00pm - 9:00pm

Location:           Jax 826 SW 2nd Ave
                    Portland, OR

The talk will be on building multiple versions of software without
unexpected adverse difficulties. (And still have it work.)

The following is the outline as provided by Eric:

INFO

Audience:
  developers
  involved administrators
  consultants / integrators
  interested others

Description:
  The talk will follow the basic outline below, quickly covering typical
  version control layouts and usage.  Fairly thorough coverage of the
  perl/python library path structure (depending on audience
  familiarity.)

  I would expect the audience to bring some familiarity with system
  administration and program installation.  Developers will probably
  benefit more than administrators, but most admins have at least
  written a bit of perl code and would definitely benefit from a less
  ad-hoc approach to this (especially if they have trouble with
  different versions of custom scripts on multiple machines.)

  I would like to break into ad-hoc discussion about extending the
  concept into compiled code and large projects.  I think the audience
  would have more thoughts on handling dependencies and dealing with
  various package management systems.  These are somewhat hairy areas,
  and the conclusion may be that you only want to use this approach when
  the complexity is easily managed.

  I think discussion of a chroot approach would fit as well.

  The "stupid question threshold" would be down around an understanding
  of filesystems and code vs binary, so anyone with a few years
  experience and no fear of the command line should be able to keep up.


OUTLINE

Motivations:
  code development
  project tracking
  casual contribution

Traditional approach:
  make && make test && make install
  what sort of troubles copies cause
  why this is tedious if you're developing interpreted code
  why this is difficult if you're tracking multiple versions

Basics:
  version control (svn/cvs/svk)
    trunk, branch, etc.
    vendor branches, external
  symlinks
  locations
    /usr/local/svn_stuff/
    /usr/local/stow/
        etc.
    $PATH
    $PERL5LIB
        $PYTHONPATH

Interpreted code:
  perl, python, ruby, lisp

Compiled code:
  C, C++

Issues:
  Dependencies
  Package management systems
  broken symlinks
  unexpected behavior?


Usual meeting rules apply. Happy Hour meal prices for the first hour. 


-- 
"All power is derived from the barrel of a GNU." - Mao Tse Stallman



From Jkarlock at earthlink.net  Tue Jul 19 16:21:58 2005
From: Jkarlock at earthlink.net (Jim Karlock)
Date: Tue, 19 Jul 2005 16:21:58 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] UNWIRE PORTLAND SCHEDULES PUBLIC WORKSHOP
Message-ID: <4.2.2.20050719162123.02d44100@mail.earthlink.net>

FOR IMMEDIATE RELEASE           CONTACT: Toni Severe Marcelin, PDC
July 11, 2005                                   503-823-3326

UNWIRE PORTLAND SCHEDULES PUBLIC WORKSHOP;
City Commissioner Sam Adams Keynote Speaker
__________________________________________________________________

A public workshop has been scheduled to provide the public an opportunity 
to learn about the Unwire Portland project and for project partners to 
gather community comment for an upcoming Request for Proposals (RFP) 
process. The workshop is scheduled for Thursday, July 28 from 5:00-7:00 
p.m. at the Oregon Association of Minority Entrepreneurs, 4134 N. Vancouver 
Avenue. City Commissioner Sam Adams will be the keynote speaker at the 
workshop.

On June 29, Portland City Council approved a proposal for a citywide 
wireless Internet network, hoping to give the city and its residents a 
lower-cost alternative to high-speed Internet services springing up across 
the metro area. The City will now issue an RFP for services on a citywide 
wireless network.

Commissioner Adams will welcome participants and talk briefly about why 
Portland City Council unanimously supports this effort. "This project will 
bring universal access to Portland, making us better connected to the world 
and better connected to each other," Commissioner Adams said. "The end 
result is increased prosperity for the city's residents, small businesses, 
schools and transit system."

City of Portland's Chief Technology Officer Matt Lampe will present 
information regarding the project mission and the RFP process. "The project 
is a great example of public agencies coming together to leverage their 
strengths to promote a new technology deployment while creating new 
commercial options for the public," said Matt Lampe.


-More-

Unwire Portland
Page 2


Attendees can find out more about the project and its benefit by visiting 
five input stations staffed by members of the Steering Committee 
representing TriMet, Portland Public Schools, small business, technology 
and city services.

The City is pursuing the development of a network through an innovative 
public-private partnership. The three core public partnersthe City of 
Portland, Portland Public Schools and TriMetdeveloped the RFP to attract a 
private company or partnership to install and manage the network using no 
new public funds. The selected network developer would build the network 
using the public partners' assets, such as street lights, traffic signals, 
school buildings or radio towers to install the wireless equipment. The 
partners would also be early users of the network, providing the developer 
revenues to support network development while providing cost-saving access 
solutions to the City and other public agencies. The network would be open 
to multiple Service Providers to provide retail Internet access for 
Portland businesses and residents.

After considering public input from the workshop, the Committee plans to 
release the RFP in late August. More information on the workshop and Unwire 
Portland can be found on the web at: www.pdc.us/unwire.  Sponsors of the 
workshop include the City of Portland's Bureau of Technology Services, 
Portland Development Commission (PDC), and the Unwire Portland Steering 
Committee. The Steering Committee is comprised of representatives from the 
Mayor's office, the offices of Commissioners Sam Adams and Erik Sten, 
Bureau of Technology Services, Alliance of Portland Neighborhood Business 
Associations, Portland Public Schools, TriMet and PDC.

From michael at mcmm.net  Wed Jul 20 22:18:51 2005
From: michael at mcmm.net (Michael Chan)
Date: Wed, 20 Jul 2005 22:18:51 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Kernel panic.  Need help!!!
In-Reply-To: <NAEMLOHDCGGNKGMHCPFGCEPMCCAA.jimwebb@charter.net>
References: <NAEMLOHDCGGNKGMHCPFGCEPMCCAA.jimwebb@charter.net>
Message-ID: <1121923131.1198.22.camel@localhost.localdomain>

On Tue, 2005-07-19 at 14:13 -0400, James H. Webb wrote:
> Aaron,
> 
> I used some canned air on the CPU fan.  Things quieted down and it pc is
> still running at this time.  Obviously, I need a new CPU fan. I found an old
> one and it still has some of the connection goop on it.  Will alcohol clean
> that off???

Can just replace only the fan itself?  Forgive me if I am wrong, but it
sounds like your replacement unit to which you are referring is a
different fan and the heat sink to which that fan is attached.
Otherwise, I'm confused as to what "goop" would be on the fan.  CPU fans
are not very expensive.

If I am correct in my inference and you want to use your alternate heat
sink/fan combo, the goop/residue you see is most likely either thermal
compound which is probably composed of a silicone and zinc oxide or the
remnants of a thermal pad which is composed of a phase-change chemical
in a binder.  In either case, the friction of you rubbing the applicator
is going to do more work than the alcohol you are applying with said
applicator, and then it will likely just push it around.  It is unlikely
that the material on your sink is alcohol-soluble.

You can take a razor blade and soft cloth and scrape/rub off the residue
as best you can, being careful to not mar the surface of the heat sink
as best as is possible.  Then reapply a very (very!) thin layer of
thermal compound.  You don't need to bother with Artic Silver or other
"high performance" compounds; the thermal benefits are not necessary for
standard applications.  CPU silicone is sufficient for most standard
uses.

By the way, do the best to keep the stuff off your hands.  It's a pain
get off of skin/clothes/pets.

Michael Chan

On Fri, 22 Jul 2005, Rich Shepard wrote:

>  I want to strip off the quotation marks and replace the ',' with ' -> '
> using python's regular expression module. What I have so far are these four
> lines:
>
>    p = re.compile('"')
>    bar = p.sub('','"')
>    q = re.compile(", ")
>    bar = q.sub(" -> ", ", ")

   Well, trial-and-error succeeds once again. This does work!

From ehem at m5p.com  Sat Jul 23 16:18:55 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Sat, 23 Jul 2005 16:18:55 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] SuSE 9.3 Install - "Searching for info file..."
In-Reply-To: <20050723190002.BAE294425@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200507232318.j6NNItmY004250@m5p.com>

>From: "Richard C. Steffens" <rsteff at comcast.net>
> I wondered about whether the burn was accurate, which is why I was 
> trying the md5sum approach to verifying the integrity. I'm puzzled by 
> the different md5sum results from two separate machines, both of which 
> are running the same version of SuSE, and thus, I assume, the same 
> version of md5sum.

Versions are not an issue with `md5sum`. MD5 is a defined algorithm the
only way to produce different results with the same data is to have a
bug. In order to do the job it is supposed to do differing versions of
`md5sum` *MUST* *NOT* produce differing results!

So this leaves the question open of what is happening. The obvious one is
that the CD wasn't quite burned within specs. Possibly a couple ones
aren't as long as they should be, or a couple zeros are too long. One
drive reads them as ones and the other as zeros. The upper layers of
error correction were successful with one drive, but the error correction
on the other drive wasn't successful (one read enough bits correctly to
compensate). This tends to point to a marginally burned CD, some drives
manage to read it correctly, other drives fail. This in turn means get a
new CD (or new drive which is better with CD-Rs).

	<42E28EF8.2070502@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <1122237780.17579.15.camel@dagon.fnordora.org>

On Sat, 2005-07-23 at 11:39 -0700, Richard C. Steffens wrote:
> Russell Senior wrote:
> 
> > Richard> Obviously, I'm grasping at straws, here. Two CD's I've gotten
> > Richard> from other sources load and install on the machine. Two CD's
> > Richard> I've downloaded and burned, load but don't install.
> > 
> > How are you burning them, exactly?
> 
> By using K3Bs image burning tool -- in other words, I don't know exactly 
> how. But, I know that it is different from just creating a data CD. If 
> you need better details of what K3B says and asks for, I'll have to 
> reboot, since after the machine's been running for awhile, K3B hangs 
> when it starts up.
> 
> I wondered about whether the burn was accurate, which is why I was 
> trying the md5sum approach to verifying the integrity. I'm puzzled by 
> the different md5sum results from two separate machines, both of which 
> are running the same version of SuSE, and thus, I assume, the same 
> version of md5sum.

If you run md5sum more than once, do you get the same result?  If you
get differing results, you need to check your memory.
(http://www.memtest86.com/ is your friend.)  I have had this happen, so
I know it is possible.

If things are hanging after a while, it sounds like you have a heat
related hardware problem.  Check memory first, since it is easiest to
replace.  Also check that all the cables are snug.  (Sometimes the
changes in temperature will cause them to work their way out of the
socket.)  If you have diagnostics for motherboard and CPU temperatures,
check those.  Sometimes it is in the bios screen at boot or through
lm_sensors.  (lm_sensors does not always work.  Depends on if it has a
chipset that is supported.)

Also make sure that your vents and fans are not clogged with dust and/or
cat fur.  

It could also be the burner flaking out.  

Another thing to check for is bad capacitors.  See if any are bulging
and/or leaking.  If they are, replace the motherboard.  (Unless you are
REAL good with a soldering iron.)

That is all I can think of at the moment...

From aaron at bavariati.org  Sun Jul 24 14:25:32 2005
From: aaron at bavariati.org (Aaron Burt)
Date: Sun, 24 Jul 2005 14:25:32 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Convert PDF to Text
In-Reply-To: <42E401C6.9090509@comcast.net>
References: <42E401C6.9090509@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <20050724212532.GJ12388@bavariati.org>

On Sun, Jul 24, 2005 at 02:01:58PM -0700, R. Haack wrote:
> I'm busy working so I haven't had the time to look but figured somebody 
> on this list would know the answer.  Is there a utility to convert a PDF 
> file to a Text file?  I have a report with headings, footers, and 
> columns that I need to convert to a text file.  Any ideas?

"pdftotext" can do that, assuming the PDF is real text rather than
bitmap images.  So can ghostview in Windows.  And Acrobat Reader will
often let you cut-and-paste text from a PDF.

In Debian and Ubuntu, pdftotext is in the xpdf-utils package.

Good luck,
  Aaron

Note Cards & Photographic Prints available at:

Contents of my user.js file:

/* Do not remove the @namespace line--it's required for correct 
functioning */
/* Set default namespace to XUL */
@namespace 
url("http://www.mozilla.org/keymaster/gatekeeper/there.is.only.xul");

/* Open hyperlinks in Mozilla Firefox */
user_pref("network.protocol-handler.app.http", 
"/home/rsteff/Downloads/firefox-installer/firefox");

user_pref("network.protocol-handler.app.https", 
"/home/rsteff/Downloads/firefox-installer/firefox");

user_pref("network.protocol-handler.app.ftp", 
"/home/rsteff/Downloads/firefox-installer/firefox"

From heinlein at madboa.com  Mon Jul 25 08:48:06 2005
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Mon, 25 Jul 2005 08:48:06 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Thunderbird Issues

On 7/25/05 7:15 AM, Richard C. Steffens wrote:
> I've switched to Thunderbird for a few features it has that I like 
> better than Konqueror -- multiple address books, better address 
> groupings, etc.
> 
> One feature that isn't working is being able to click on a link and have 
> it open in a browser. I found some instructions that said to create a 
> user.js file. If I understood it correctly, it wants to find that file 
> in the same directory as the program file. I have one there, but it 
> still doesn't work. The contents of the file are below.

The user.js file lives in the thunderbird profile directory in $HOME. On 
a Linux box, the path would be something like

* $HOME/.thunderbird/ptvdt5yx.default/user.js

Under OS X, it's

* $HOME/Library/Thunderbird/Profiles/tt69vp2w.default/user.js

The actual name of your profile directory will be slightly different.

Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> www.madboa.com

Blacklist of what?  You ain't paying me enough to read your mind, man.

> I would like to be able to maintain the blacklist in much the same way that
> bookmarks are maintained.

If you mean a blacklist of websites, I'm sure you could use Adblocker
in FireFox, and there may even be an extension especially for the
purpose.  Of course, someone who's even mildly technical (e.g. nearly
anyone younger than 18) would probably be able to find a way around it.
See: https://addons.mozilla.org

If you need a real web-filtering system, use DansGuardian, either on
the box as a daemon or on a separate router.  (I think IPCop supports it.)

From ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net  Mon Jul 25 09:32:49 2005
From: ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Mon, 25 Jul 2005 09:32:49 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Blacklist in Browser?
In-Reply-To: <B0012024711@bct-mail.bctonline.com>
References: <B0012024711@bct-mail.bctonline.com>
Message-ID: <200507250932.50021.ewilhelm@sbcglobal.net>

# from Charles Sliger
# on Monday 25 July 2005 09:13 am:

>A blacklist of web sites.
>It would be nice to be able to add/remove sites and organize them just
> like you do with the bookmarks. ?Then the browser would not follow a
> link or redirect to a URL on the blacklist, probably just putting out
> a warning instead.

Most browsers have a "Bookmarks" toolbar button.  Do you think that they 
should have a "Blacklist" button too?  Besides, you don't need to sort 
your blacklists by directories do you?

(heh. click Blacklist -> "Blacklist This Page")

Privoxy is a good filtering proxy.  I don't think you want to replicate 
this functionality in a browser just for the sake of having a menu 
item.  Maybe you could hack the mozilla or konqueror code to have a 
right-click menu item "blacklist image location" that would send the 
info to privoxy.

In the default setup, privoxy uses regular expressions and prefabricated 
blacklists that catch most of the junk.  You can also whitelist.  All 
of this is in text files, so you just edit them with a visual text 
editor ;-)

Now, if all of this is too inconvenient, you could make a "Blacklist" 
bookmarks folder and have dnotify or FAM (or cron if you're that 
patient) watching your bookmarks file with a perl script mirroring 
everything from that bookmark folder into the privoxy blacklist 
configs.  Repeat for a Whitelist folder (and maybe one for regex's 
too. :-)  Note the tasty *nix flavor.  Too bad bookmarks are usually 
not-so-tasty XML instead of some more filesystemish approach (that 
would let all users on a system symlink to shared global folders (not 
to mention rsync!))

--Eric

Contents of user.js:

/* Do not remove the @namespace line--it's required for correct 
functioning */
/* Set default namespace to XUL */
@namespace 
url("http://www.mozilla.org/keymaster/gatekeeper/there.is.only.xul");

/* Open hyperlinks in Mozilla Firefox */
user_pref("network.protocol-handler.app.http", 
"/home/rsteff/Downloads/firefox-installer/firefox");

user_pref("network.protocol-handler.app.https", 
"/home/rsteff/Downloads/firefox-installer/firefox");

user_pref("network.protocol-handler.app.ftp", 
"/home/rsteff/Downloads/firefox-installer/firefox");

to work at something besides VESA 1024 x 768. Never 
succeeded. Gave up and returned the laptop to HP. Instead I

From ckonstan at lunarlogic.com  Mon Jul 25 17:42:56 2005
From: ckonstan at lunarlogic.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Mon, 25 Jul 2005 17:42:56 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Linux: ATI or nVidia?
In-Reply-To: <42E52224.16118.80CD474D@localhost>
References: <42E52224.16118.80CD474D@localhost>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0507251737170.6162@localhost>

I don't have any ATI experience in linux either.  But nvidia has always
been a breeze, and support for the glx driver is in most package
management systems, like portage, apt, etc.  Or you can get the driver
from nvidia's website, and run it with the --force-update switch,
meaninng you never have to get a new driver to keep up to date - running
the old one always gets you the latest driver with NO brain-time.  I run
it every time I build a new kernel (because I have to, as it is a kernel
module).

I think the nvidia driver also supports AMD64.  It sure seemed that way
when I installed it on this 64 bit box they gave me at work.  500 fps -
wow!

Carlos

From shahms at shahms.com  Mon Jul 25 17:51:22 2005
From: shahms at shahms.com (Shahms E. King)
Date: Mon, 25 Jul 2005 17:51:22 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Linux: ATI or nVidia?
In-Reply-To: <20050726000914.75041.qmail@web52612.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20050726000914.75041.qmail@web52612.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <1122339082.31139.7.camel@home.shahms.com>

On Mon, 2005-07-25 at 17:09 -0700, Scott Van Hoosen wrote:
> I'm looking to buy a new video card, something with some nice 3D
> capabilities. I've always bought nVidia cards in the past, but I'm
> wondering if ATI would be as good or better for Linux. It seems like
> you get more bang for the buck with ATI now, but I'm not sure (I
> haven't been up on video cards for a couple years). I know nVidia has
> closed-source, downloadable drivers for Linux. How are ATI's drivers
> handled?

ATI cards with 3D supported by the open-source drivers (mostly older
Radeons) are the best option.  If you want a newer card, the fglrx
drivers suck ass.  They are horribly unstable and a general PITA.  The
nVidia binary drivers are much, much, much better.


--Shahms

From ehem at m5p.com  Mon Jul 25 18:28:00 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Mon, 25 Jul 2005 18:28:00 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Linux: ATI or nVidia?
In-Reply-To: <20050726001614.A000143BF@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200507260128.j6Q1S063046969@m5p.com>

>From: Scott Van Hoosen <svanhoosen at yahoo.com>
> I'm looking to buy a new video card, something with some nice 3D
> capabilities. I've always bought nVidia cards in the past, but I'm
> wondering if ATI would be as good or better for Linux. It seems like
> you get more bang for the buck with ATI now, but I'm not sure (I
> haven't been up on video cards for a couple years). I know nVidia has
> closed-source, downloadable drivers for Linux. How are ATI's drivers
> handled?

Generally ATi is slightly more power per dollar, but notorious for bad
drivers. nVIDIA is legendary for high-quality drivers (both Linux and
less-abled "OSes"). If you want the 3D capabilities then you'll be a
slave to the binary drivers, luckily both companies offer them.

nVIDIA's GF5### chips turned out to be a lemon generation, somewhat
faster but not really much better than the GF4### chips (but they still
had good drivers). The more recent GF6### and GF7### cards look to be
extremely good though. ATi's R9### chips were an awesome generation, but
they've been followed by the unimpressive RX### chips. At the moment
ATi's X800 is now a generation behind nVIDIA's GF7880, in theory they
should be coming out with something soon but that was originally expected
*months* ago.

> Suppose you wanted to spend $150 or less on a good video card for
> Linux, which card on ENU's list would you buy:
> 
> http://www.enuinc.com/vgx.html

If your motherboard supports PCIe cards, the MSI NX6600-TD256E is a
mid-end one generation back card. Otherwise it seems that ENU's selection
of nVIDIA cards is rather sparse right now.  :-(

From ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net  Mon Jul 25 18:32:06 2005
From: ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net (Eric Wilhelm)

Subject: [PLUG] Linux: ATI or nVidia?

# from Shahms E. King
# on Monday 25 July 2005 05:51 pm:

>ATI cards with 3D supported by the open-source drivers (mostly older
>Radeons) are the best option. ?If you want a newer card ...

Wow. ATI actually made an effort to support their cards on Linux.  That 
puts them at least a few years behind nvidia, and of course it's a 
proprietary driver.

In either case, your kernel will be tainted (causes trouble if you're 
reporting kernel bugs.)  Guess there's some tasty IP tangled into that 
driver code that keeps them from opening it.

>nVidia binary drivers are much, much, much better.

At least they've been releasing them for Linux longer.  That's why I 
went with nvidia 2.5 years ago (wow, I guess this dual 4800 is a 
dinosaur now!)  I get some crashes, but it's hard to say whether that 
comes from the motherboard, onboard sound, usb, smp, xinerama, or that 
PCI TNT2 card running the third monitor.  Probably a combination of 
things (something about running out of IRQ's)  If you're going 
single-head and single-cpu, then nvidia is pretty stable.

One caveat:  nvidia doesn't produce their own boards.  They only do the 
chips, so there will be plenty of various brands selling boards with 
nvidia chips.  These are not all created equal!  Namely, MSI is really 
bad.  I'll just take another opportunity to say "stay away from MSI."

MSI is really bad.

BTW, Do not buy an MSI graphics card (or anything else for that matter.)

Look for a card manufacturer with firmware on their website (last I 
looked nvidia says to get the firmware from the card manufacturer.)  
Low quality outfits (like MSI) tell you to get the firmware updates 
from nvidia.

Fans and other bits also fail (or make noise) on cheaper cards.  You get 
what you pay for.

Could anyone with a more pleasant nvidia experience name some quality 
card manufacturers?

--Eric

From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Mon Jul 25 20:22:17 2005
From: wcooley at nakedape.cc (Wil Cooley)
Date: Mon, 25 Jul 2005 20:22:17 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Python docs for string manipulation?
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.62.0507221145090.11194@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.62.0507221145090.11194@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <1122348138.3289.4.camel@denk.nakedape.cc>

On Fri, 2005-07-22 at 11:48 -0700, Rich Shepard wrote:
>    Looking at the docs for python-2.4 I cannot find a dictionary of what can
> be done with strings. For example, in the doc for the RE module is the
> suggestion that replacement of a single character can be quicker using the
> .translate() function on a string. However, I cannot find a list of functions
> that operate on strings, and how they're called. The 'string' module has been
> deprecated but the library reference has a short section on that module.
> 
>    I know two other string functions are .split() and .join(). But, where's
> the documentation for these and others to be found?

The quick and easy way to find answers to questions like these is to
fire up the interactive interpreter and use the built-in dir() function:

$ python
Python 2.4.1 (#1, May 16 2005, 15:19:29) 
[GCC 4.0.0 20050512 (Red Hat 4.0.0-5)] on linux2
Type "help", "copyright", "credits" or "license" for more information.
>>> dir('')
['__add__', '__class__', '__contains__', '__delattr__', '__doc__',
'__eq__', '__ge__', '__getattribute__', '__getitem__', '__getnewargs__',
'__getslice__', '__gt__', '__hash__', '__init__', '__le__', '__len__',
'__lt__', '__mod__', '__mul__', '__ne__', '__new__', '__reduce__',
'__reduce_ex__', '__repr__', '__rmod__', '__rmul__', '__setattr__',
'__str__', 'capitalize', 'center', 'count', 'decode', 'encode',
'endswith', 'expandtabs', 'find', 'index', 'isalnum', 'isalpha',
'isdigit', 'islower', 'isspace', 'istitle', 'isupper', 'join', 'ljust',
'lower', 'lstrip', 'replace', 'rfind', 'rindex', 'rjust', 'rsplit',
'rstrip', 'split', 'splitlines', 'startswith', 'strip', 'swapcase',
'title', 'translate', 'upper', 'zfill']

(The empty string '' is an instance of a string, so dir('') tells you
all the methods defined for the class.  Try also "dir({})" and "dir([])"
for added fun.)

Wil

From znmeb at cesmail.net  Mon Jul 25 22:04:21 2005
From: znmeb at cesmail.net (M. Edward (Ed) Borasky)

Subject: [PLUG] Perl Question

References: <250ae432d9c806e4d7855f3f0f7224dc@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <42E5C455.3030402@cesmail.net>

Doug Davis wrote:

> I know there are a lot of Perl experts here, so I thought I would ask 
> about a problem I have.
>
> I have a very large file that is exported from an application. Its all 
> one line and more than 3000 characters so sed/awk bails out on me, I 
> suggested Perl might be a good choice, but we are having problems with 
> the regex matching. There are no delimiters, but each field starts 
> with a constant prefix and is a fixed length.
>
> What I want to do in English is to find this string plus the next 80 
> characters (combination of text and whitespace, and replace it with 
> the same string + a replacement string + fill the remaining spaces 
> with whitespace. What's the best way to do this? Just to give you a 
> point of reference, we are replacing actual customer names with 
> something like John Doe.

Ah ... yes. Something like

$hugestring =~ s/NAME=.{80}/NAME=${newname}/g;

where "$newname" contains "John Doe" followed by 72 spaces, etc.

The context indicates you've been given some kind of database dump, 
sadly not the traditional comma-separated or tab-separated value format 
with text strings enclosed in quotes and terminated by newlines. Is it 
possible to get the application to export in such a format, which would 
make this a rather simple loop?

I'm also guessing you don't want to replace every person's name with 
"John Doe" but a different name for each original name. So rather than 
use a one-shot replace command, you somehow might need to break the 
string up into individual records, replace each name field with a random 
one, then reassemble the string. Is that correct? If so, is there any 
kind of "record separator" in your input string?

Finally, do you need to re-import the resulting string back into the 
application?

I have a working vgetty and a working mgetty configuration.  The 
default for vgetty is voice:fax:data.  I truncated that to voice 
because I don't want a caller to get a modem in their ear.  Is 
there a way to allow the caller to indicate that a modem call is 
coming and have mgetty answer the next call instead?  Is there a 
way to implement a dial menu with vgetty, press 1 for modem call, 
2 to leave a message?  The ability to leave a message is an 
improvement, but I want to do full blown remote control.

One option, if this can be done, is to record a person requesting
modem service, record them saying modem for example. I'm thinking
do a comparison between the last message and that recording.
So you call and vgetty asks for a message.  You say modem
after the tone and hang up.  A daemon sees that there is a new
message and compares it to a recording of you saying modem made 
earlier.  If there is a match, init is set to call mgetty 
instead and restarted.  If there's an easier approach to solving
this problem that anyone has implemented using vgetty, I'd love 
to hear about it.  

Anyone know of a simple way with vgetty to interpret touch tones 
as commands?  I call and vgetty answers, I want to be able
to press a series of numbers and have vgetty interpret them as
a signal that I want to make a data call.  I'm thinking after
I hang up that a script called by vgetty can switch the modem
to use mgetty instead for like the next ten minutes.

From rich at paranoid.org  Wed Jul 20 17:11:54 2005
From: rich at paranoid.org (Rich Burroughs)
Date: Wed, 20 Jul 2005 17:11:54 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Knoweldge base apps
Message-ID: <30784.70.57.126.130.1121904714.squirrel@o4.hostbaby.com>

From nickaubert at gmail.com  Tue Jul 26 09:17:01 2005
From: nickaubert at gmail.com (Nick Aubert)
Date: Tue, 26 Jul 2005 09:17:01 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Knoweldge base apps
In-Reply-To: <30784.70.57.126.130.1121904714.squirrel@o4.hostbaby.com>
References: <30784.70.57.126.130.1121904714.squirrel@o4.hostbaby.com>
Message-ID: <55ef240d050726091748e1b84c@mail.gmail.com>

With most wikis, you can restrict which users are allowed to make
updates.  So if it's the wikis' openness to modification by the
general public that's turning you off, you might want to look into
using a wiki anyway.  You can configure your wiki so that only you or
people you've selected are allowed to make changes, with read-only
access for everyone else.

You can download wikipedia's engine from sourceforge here:
http://sourceforge.net/projects/wikipedia
It needs a MySQL backend.  It's developed for Linux, but since it's
written in PHP, it shouldn't be too problematic to get it running on
Solaris.

Here's a list of other wiki engines: 
http://c2.com/cgi/wiki?WikiEngines

I know you said you said that you weren't really looking for a wiki,
but you haven't said why not.  I'm not sure what your needs are, so
I'm suggesting that a wiki might still suit your situation.  Arguably,
editing html files in vi constitutes a knowledge base app.

From ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net  Tue Jul 26 09:56:59 2005
From: ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Tue, 26 Jul 2005 09:56:59 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Perl Question
In-Reply-To: <42E5C455.3030402@cesmail.net>
References: <250ae432d9c806e4d7855f3f0f7224dc@gmail.com>
	<42E5C455.3030402@cesmail.net>
Message-ID: <200507260956.59526.ewilhelm@sbcglobal.net>

# from M. Edward (Ed) Borasky
# on Monday 25 July 2005 10:04 pm:

>$hugestring =~ s/NAME=.{80}/NAME=${newname}/g;
>
>where "$newname" contains "John Doe" followed by 72 spaces, etc.

>I'm also guessing you don't want to replace every person's name with
>"John Doe" but a different name for each original name. So rather than
>use a one-shot replace command, you somehow might need to break the
>string up into individual records, replace each name field with a
> random one, then reassemble the string. Is that correct? If so, is
> there any kind of "record separator" in your input string?

Or you can add the 'e' modifier and call a function.

  $hugestring =~ s/NAME=.{80}/
	"NAME=" . make_newname($1)/ex;

Check 'perldoc perlre'.

Of course, you might have a performance issue if $hugestring is that 
huge.  Not sure if you would get a better result using substr() within 
a loop there or not.

I'm looking for a slick ( one-liner? ) to test if a smbfs is mounted.

I have scripts that mount shares from Win2K servers and process data
files.  Sometimes _stuff(s**t) happens_ and they get mounted twice or

again and if for some reason the share has been mounted multiple times I 
can umount it multiple times.

I've gone over the man pages for test and umount but nothing I tried
worked the way I hoped.  That is just looking for the mount not testing
for some file in the share which can be problematic.

Ideas?

From eli.stair at gmail.com  Tue Jul 26 10:46:51 2005
From: eli.stair at gmail.com (Eli Stair)
Date: Tue, 26 Jul 2005 11:46:51 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] File test for _mounted_ CIF/SMB filesystem
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0507261010450.31005-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0507261010450.31005-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
Message-ID: <f4468cae05072610476aea81c8@mail.gmail.com>

Try either autofs (4.x) or just a cron job or somesuch that does
something along the lines of:

cat /proc/mounts | grep smbfs | grep $MOUNTPOINT | grep -v grep >
/dev/null  || (MOUNT COMMAND)

/eli

From raanders at acm.org  Tue Jul 26 13:11:02 2005
From: raanders at acm.org (Roderick A. Anderson)
Date: Tue, 26 Jul 2005 13:11:02 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] File test for _mounted_ CIF/SMB filesystem
In-Reply-To: <f4468cae05072610476aea81c8@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0507261303560.32417-100000@main.cyber-office.net>

On Tue, 26 Jul 2005, Eli Stair wrote:

> Try either autofs (4.x) or just a cron job or somesuch that does
> something along the lines of:
> 
> cat /proc/mounts | grep smbfs | grep $MOUNTPOINT | grep -v grep >
> /dev/null  || (MOUNT COMMAND)

This works great.  And incase some brain-dead bozo developer ( me ) gets 
on the system and mounts the file system then forgets to un-mount it; 
this, based on your suggestion, works.

while $(cat /proc/mounts | grep smbfs | grep $MOUNTPOINT ) ; \
    do umount $MOUNTPOINT ; done

Thanks Eli.


Rod

From rsteff at comcast.net  Tue Jul 26 16:01:34 2005
From: rsteff at comcast.net (Richard C. Steffens)
Date: Tue, 26 Jul 2005 16:01:34 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Resolved: Thunderbird Issues
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.62.0507251516300.2140@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0507251447320.25224-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
	<Pine.LNX.4.62.0507251516300.2140@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <42E6C0CE.4080005@comcast.net>

Rich Shepard wrote:

> A google search for "+thunderbird +url" returned 678,000 hits. On the 
> first page is this: 
> <http://gentoo-wiki.com/TIP_Integrate_Thunderbird_and_Firefox>,
> and it includes:
> 
> "Open URLs in Firefox from Thunderbird
> 
> "To change the behaviour of Thunderbird you have to edit the file
> ~/.thunderbird/<something>.default/prefs.js and adding the following lines:
> File: ~/.thunderbird/<something>.default/prefs.js
> 
> "user_pref("network.protocol-handler.app.ftp","/usr/bin/firefox");
> "user_pref("network.protocol-handler.app.http", "/usr/bin/firefox");
> "user_pref("network.protocol-handler.app.https", "/usr/bin/firefox");"

I found something similar by chasing it through Mozilla's site. But what 
they said was to put those lines in a separate file, user.js.

Here's what's at the top of my prefs.js file:

/* Do not edit this file.
  *
  * If you make changes to this file while the browser is running,
  * the changes will be overwritten when the browser exits.
  *
  * To make a manual change to preferences, you can visit the URL
about:config
  * For more information, see
http://www.mozilla.org/unix/customizing.html#prefs
  */

So, I ignored the "Do not edit" instruction and put those three lines, 
with appropriate changes for my installation, at the bottom of the 
prefs.js file, and now it works!

"Do it THIS way, unless I meant something else." This is starting to 
feel like that comment about standards, "The great thing about standards 
is that there are so many to choose from."

Another thing that doesn't make sense about the comment section above: 
visit the URL about:config? That make sense for Firefox, and indeed 
works, but the concept of visiting a URL with Thunderbird doesn't make 
sense to me. I wonder if this is a comment that belongs in the Mozilla 
combined product, and not in Thunderbird.

Well, thanks to the persistence of many, I have links working in 
Thunderbird. Thanks to all.

On Tue, Jul 26, 2005 at 12:51:50PM -0700, Rich Burroughs wrote:
> On Tue, July 26, 2005 12:01 pm, Rich Shepard wrote:
> > "Knowledge base" is quite vague. What will be stored and how will
> > it be used?
> 
> I don't think it's a vague term for at all for people who work in IT.

Hrmpf.  Most folks with the IT background to answer that have also
suffered the painful consequences of jumping to conclusions about what
a person means when they say they want $BUZZWORD. ;)

> I'm looking for a place to store operations policies and procedures. An
> example of an entry might be a common problem, and the workaround or fix.

The RT FAQ Manager may be a good fit; integration between trouble-
tickets and knowledge base really facilitates knowledge-capture.
http://www.bestpractical.com/rtfm/

Note that if you are running a support/service org and you're *not*
using a trouble-ticket system already, get one in place post-haste.
RT is a good one, and its search capabilites make it an effective
knowledge-manager by itself.

> A wiki would work for what I'm suggesting, but I don't want to use a wiki.
> Call it personal preference.

Okeedokee.  I'll note that of all the knowledge-base-type sites I
refer to on the net, all but LDP are Wikis.

From mikeraz at patch.com  Wed Jul 27 06:25:15 2005
From: mikeraz at patch.com (Michael Rasmussen)
Date: Wed, 27 Jul 2005 06:25:15 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] File test for _mounted_ CIF/SMB filesystem
In-Reply-To: <f4468cae05072610476aea81c8@mail.gmail.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0507261010450.31005-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
	<f4468cae05072610476aea81c8@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20050727132514.GB10206@patch.com>

Eli Stair wrote:
> Try either autofs (4.x) or just a cron job or somesuch that does
> something along the lines of:
> 
> cat /proc/mounts | grep smbfs | grep $MOUNTPOINT | grep -v grep >
> /dev/null  || (MOUNT COMMAND)

or perhaps

grep $MOUNTPOINT /proc/mounts || action if not mounted
grep $MOUNTPOINT /proc/mounts && action if mounted

depending on which logical construct better fits what you're doing.

for umounting when you have multiples 

if [`grep -c $MOUNTPOINT /proc/mounts` > 1 ]; do umount $MOUNTPOINT; done

should do fine.

> > I have scripts that mount shares from Win2K servers and process data
> > files.  Sometimes _stuff(s**t) happens_ and they get mounted twice or
> > more.  I prefer to not leave them mounted all the time as the processing
> > times are sparse.

From mcintoshrt at gmail.com  Wed Jul 27 10:12:13 2005
From: mcintoshrt at gmail.com (Robert McIntosh)
Date: Wed, 27 Jul 2005 10:12:13 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] http -> https redirect
Message-ID: <42E7C06D.4030407@comcast.net>

Hi,

I'm trying to get apache to redirect http requests on a subdirectory,
say http://www.mysite.com/subdir to redirect it to
https://www.mysite.com/subdir.

I've found a nice .htaccess statement to put in the ./subdir directory:

<IfModule !mod_ssl.c>
Redirect permanent / https://www.mysite.com/
</IfModule>

Apache (2.0.x) isn't paying attention to it, even though in httpd.conf
AllowOverride is set to "All".

This seems like a fairly typical thing to have to do, yet I'm stumped.

Please help.

TIA,
Robert

Robert McIntosh
mcintoshrt at gmail.com


From rlucas at tercent.com  Wed Jul 27 10:48:00 2005
From: rlucas at tercent.com (Randall Lucas)
Date: Wed, 27 Jul 2005 10:48:00 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Unwire Portland public meeting tomorrow
Message-ID: <42E7C8D0.7060007@tercent.com>

The city's project for enabling citywide wireless access -- the Unwire
Portland project -- is holding a public meeting tomorrow (Thursday, 28
July) from 5-7 at OAME, 4134 N. Vancouver, Portland.

Part of the project's requirements is that the implementation give a
public benefit.  Right now, the leading proposal is the "walled garden,"
where a restricted list of sites is made available.

An alternative idea, the "drinking fountain" model, proposes to give
free, unrestricted but low-bandwidth access to all comers.  (See
http://rlucas.tercent.com/wifi.html for my position on the issue.)
I think that the Linux community (with a natural affinity for
information-dense [text] network uses) stands to gain a lot if the
drinking fountain model is adopted.

There will definitely be politicos and commercial vendors there.  It
would be outstanding if we could get some strong representation from the
F/OSS and Linux communities there as well.

Official PDF on the meeting:
http://www.pdc.us/unwire/workshop-flyer_7-28-05.pdf

-- 
Randall Lucas            DF93EAD1
Tercent, Inc / SuperSurvey Online Surveys
http://www.supersurvey.com

From eli.stair at gmail.com  Wed Jul 27 11:10:59 2005
From: eli.stair at gmail.com (Eli Stair)
Date: Wed, 27 Jul 2005 12:10:59 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] http -> https redirect
In-Reply-To: <42E7C06D.4030407@comcast.net>
References: <42E7C06D.4030407@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <f4468cae050727111163b6bb25@mail.gmail.com>

I just have a default vhost that does:

<VirtualHost *:80>
 ServerAdmin webmaster at FQDN
 ServerName FQDN

    # DocumentRoot: The directory out of which you will serve your
    # documents. By default, all requests are taken from this directory, but
    # symbolic links and aliases may be used to point to other locations.
 DocumentRoot /srv/www/vhosts/disc.ont.inuo.us/htdocs


Redirect / https://FQDN/


....

Then have a ssl vhost:

(among other things does:)

<VirtualHost _default_:443>

        DocumentRoot "/srv/www/vhosts/ssl-default/htdocs"
        ServerName FQDN:443

...

Hope this helps in your case, if not let me know and I can look at
your configs with you.

/eli

From raanders at acm.org  Wed Jul 27 11:46:05 2005
From: raanders at acm.org (Roderick A. Anderson)
Date: Wed, 27 Jul 2005 11:46:05 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] File test for _mounted_ CIF/SMB filesystem
In-Reply-To: <20050727132514.GB10206@patch.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0507271054320.8966-100000@main.cyber-office.net>

On Wed, 27 Jul 2005, Michael Rasmussen wrote:

> or perhaps
> 
> grep $MOUNTPOINT /proc/mounts || action if not mounted
> grep $MOUNTPOINT /proc/mounts && action if mounted

Man is my mind somewhere else.  Yes this is way better.  Thanks!

> depending on which logical construct better fits what you're doing.
> 
> for umounting when you have multiples 
> 
> if [`grep -c $MOUNTPOINT /proc/mounts` > 1 ]; do umount $MOUNTPOINT; done
> 
> should do fine.

My mind actually is full.  This doesn't work nor variations of it.  I 
finally went with:

while $(grep $mount /proc/mounts > /dev/null mount $MNTDIR/$mount ; done

FYI, there are multiple mounts/shares so this is wrapped in a for ; do 
; done loop and that is where $mount comes from.

Again, thanks for the code.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Wed Jul 27 12:47:37 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Wed, 27 Jul 2005 12:47:37 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] http -> https redirect
In-Reply-To: <42E7C06D.4030407@comcast.net>
References: <42E7C06D.4030407@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <20050727194737.GA14472@gate.kl-ic.com>

On Wed, Jul 27, 2005 at 10:12:13AM -0700, Robert McIntosh wrote:
> Hi,
> 
> I'm trying to get apache to redirect http requests on a subdirectory,
> say http://www.mysite.com/subdir to redirect it to
> https://www.mysite.com/subdir.

-------------------------------------------

When I connect to ssh.keithl.com, it hooks me up to an ssh terminal
window.  Here's what I do in my httpd.conf : 

...

<VirtualHost *:80>
   ServerName ssh.keithl.com
   ServerAlias mail.keithl.com ssh.launchloop.com mail.launchloop.com
   Redirect / https://ssh.keithl.com/
</VirtualHost>

<VirtualHost *:443>
   ServerName ssh.keithl.com
   DocumentRoot /home/www/html/
   ...

</VirtualHost>

...

-------------------------------------------

I hope that helps.

Keith

From jeme at brelin.net  Wed Jul 27 15:58:54 2005
From: jeme at brelin.net (Jeme A Brelin)

Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0507271549230.29950@shaft.bitmine.net>


On Wed, 27 Jul 2005, Randal L. Schwartz wrote:
> Call me skeptical, but I don't think the voices of "unfiltered access" 
> will ever weigh above the right wingers.  Not in this current political 
> climate.  Not when Janet Jackson's nipple and GTA:SA's pixellated game 
> mod are making front-page news.

You're confusing the media establishment and Portland.  They're not the 
same thing.

The public policies of the city of Portland reflect the desires of the 
people to an astonishing degree.  And the people of Portland support 
freedom, openness, and sharing.

Remember that "government" governs behavior, but public agencies are not 
all government.  The public library system is not "the government" because 
they don't tell you what to do (though the library is governed by those 
who decide how to govern the people).

So, government bad -- public resources good.

The City of Portland is going to build a city-wide wireless network of 
undetermined freedom and openness.  However this is constructed, private 
agents will still have the option of offering wireless services 
(overlapping coverage happens all the time), so the public service will 
not prohibit "better" services offered by the private sector.

But at the moment, the City is considering using a private agency for 
design, management, and maintenance of the city-wide network.  If this 
happens, public money will be directly tagged as profits for this private 
agency.  Instead, we can use 100% of the budget for the project to pay 
workers and buy/maintain equipment directly.  Furthermore, a private 
agency running the citywide network will increase the chances of services 
being restricted from free use either so that they can be sold for some 
upgrade charge or to prevent litigation.  A public service would have no 
motivation to limit service based on profit motives and much less 
reason to fear litigation.

J.

From merlyn at stonehenge.com  Wed Jul 27 18:06:57 2005

Date: 27 Jul 2005 18:06:57 -0700
